11/1/2012 12:30:44 AM

Dear Gene.

As promised, this is my explanation as to the optimizations I
used for O3 in 2010 and MET-24 in 2011, both of which, of course,
draw on the basic parapyth 2.3.7.11.13 subset of George Secor's
29-HTT (1978), secor29htt.scl.

The parameters for O3, actually designed in 1024-EDO, are
theoretically (2/1, 703.893, 57.148 cents), with the generator
very close to that of POTE Parapyth (2/1, 703.856, 58.339).
However, the logic may be a bit different, and it's my purpose
here to explain that, rather than get into possible RMP questions
or interpretations, which we can do in our dialogue.

The parameters for MET-24, mainly designed to improve 3/2 and 9/8
a bit as well as to strike as equal a balance between 14/13 and
11/10, are a theoretical (2/1, 703.711, 57.422). This is an
interesting example where the structure of 1024-EDO itself
pointed to the choice of generator (actually the average of two
generators in the real-world tuning), but there's a theoretical
way of reaching an almost identical result not tied to any
specific EDO. We might speak of these as the "bitmap" and
"vectorized" versions, if an analogy from computer graphics might
be helpful.

I've decided to reserve the question of an alternative
optimization with the generator of the 7/6-13/9-26/21 eigenmonzo
tuning you called to my attention (2/1, 703.782, 59.308) for
another post, because this question deserves more consideration
on my part. Thus this post will stick with O3 and MET-24.

What I should emphasize at the outset, before explaining the
optimization of these tunings, is one point about O3 as well as
the later MET-24.

Both tunings are very specifically designed to optimize the 11/10
neutral second, as well as 12/11, 13/12, and 14/13. That was a
major focus of O3 as well as MET-24, as I made clear in my
announcement of O3:

</tuning/topicId_91499.html#91499>

In that announcement, I noted a specific desire for a system
"optimizing the large Zalzalian or neutral third at 26/21 (370
cents)" for an historical flavor of Ottoman Rast. "More
generally," I continued, "it was my goal to optimize all four of
the [superparticular] Zalzalian or middle second steps discussed
by medieval Islamic theorists such as Safi al-Din, and also Ozan,
the 14:13, 13:12, 12:11, and 11:10."

One interesting cultural point here is that 26/21 is a basic
interval for me, and might go far to define a tuning system, once
I make clear my implicit assumption that this interval will be
the diminished fourth from 8 generators up.

At the same time, I was drawn to idea of a just 22/21 limma,
another ratio I really like. And, of course, 14/13 and 13/11
would be important, as well as 7/6, 7/4, 9/7, and 21/16, etc.

----------------------------------------------------------------
1. Optimizing O3 in 1024-EDO: Some help from the limma for 11/10 ----------------------------------------------------------------

For O3 in 1024-EDO, my goal within a single 12-MOS chain was to
get 26/21 close to just and at the same time have 11/10 with
roughly Secor's HTT tolerance of just, 3.247 cents, which since
2001, when he shared that tuning with me, has become a kind of
emblem of "near-just" quality.

This brings me to what may be a basic difference between the POTE
worldview and my optimization strategy.

The POTE, I assume, looks at all relevant primes at the same
time, and gives them weights by which to arrive, say, at a rank-3
Parapyth system with the parameters simultaneously determined.

In my approach, it's more of a layered process: first optimizing
a 12-MOS or its slightly irregular equivalent in 1024-EDO; and
then deciding on the spacing which will complete a rank-3,
24-note tuning.

My approach is somewhat analogous to the layered or successive
composition of 13th-14th century European polyphony, where often
one voice is added at a time. Indeed, one might often start with
an existing melody, and add one or more new melodic lines to it.
This is what happened in Peppermint-24: Keenan Pepper had already
defined the 12-MOS, and I simply picked the distance at which to
set the second identical chain (58.680 cents) for a pure 7/6.
There neither the 12-MOS of Keenan Pepper nor the spacing was
conceived in 1024-EDO, but O3 was designed from the ground up
specifically for 1024-EDO.

This means that for O3, I first designed and optimized the basic
rank-2 12-MOS, and then decided on the spacing. Both stages of
the process were based in 1024-EDO, as I'll describe.

Here I realized that a just 22/21 and 26/21 were highly
compatible ideas; if asked to explain, I might note that the
difference between these intervals is 13/11, which in O3 is
always within a cent of just.

Another element of the 12-MOS equation for O3, and also for
MET-24 as we'll see, is the subtle balance between 14/13 and
11/10, the two epimoric neutral seconds represented within a
single chain of generators. I knew that 14/13 would be a bit
narrow at a just 22/21 tuning, but still well within the HTT
tolerance: 11/10 was more the issue.

Of course, I knew that the theoretical generator was
(84/11)^(1/5) or 3/2 tempered wide by (896/891)^(1/5), at 703.893
cents. Rather humorously, this is 1.938 cents wide, or almost
precisely as impure as in 12n-EDO (1.955 cents), but in the
opposite direction!

In practice, however, I was designing and tuning in 1024-EDO,
where there is no fifth of this size, but available nearby sizes
of 600 or 601 steps: 703.125 or 704.297 cents. My purpose was
develop a bearing plan so that, if possible, all limmas or
diatonic semitones from 5 fifths down would be at the best
possible approximation of 22/21.

This approximation was 69 steps, or 80.859 cents -- wide of 22/21
by 0.322 cents. The reason for this slight difference from just
(80.537 cents) is that while 599 steps is almost exactly 3/2, the
representation of 896/891 at 8 steps (9.375 cents) falls slightly
short of the just size at 9.688 cents.

My strategy was to lay out a digital "bearing plan" so that each
five generators in a chain would be wide by 8 tuning steps in all
for the best 22/21. I'll first give the scheme, and then consider
the consequences for 11/10.

704.3 703.1 704.3 703.1 704.3 704.3 703.1 704.3 703.1 704.3 704.3
Eb Bb F C G D A E B F# C# G#
601 600 601 600 601 601 600 601 600 601 601
+2 +1 +2 +1 +2 +2 +1 +2 +1 +2 +2

One compromise of this scheme, by the way, is that although the
average temperament might be a bit less in than 12n-EDO, 7 or our
11 fifths in a chain are a bit more impure than in 12n-EDO. But
that's an aside: let's get back to 11/10.

Because of the slight inaccuracy of 1024-EDO in the wide direction
for 22/21, and our consistent use of this closest approximation
at 69 tuning steps or 80.859 cents, it follows that 11/10 from
two such limmas, or a chain of ten fifths down, will be a bit
larger than (22/21)^2 or 484/441 at 161.074 cents -- i.e. 138
tuning steps or 161.719 cents, about 3.285 cents narrow of 11/10.
This is very close to the emblematic HTT standard of 3.247
cents, and so I deemed it a happy optimization.

Another feature of this optimization is that 13/11 is always
within a cent of just (289.210 cents), at either 4 or 5 tuning
steps narrow of the near-just 1024-EDO version of 32/27 at 251
tuning steps: 288.281 cents or 289.453 cents.

How about our 26/21 with a just size of 369.747 cents (thinking
of airlines helps to remember the decimal value!)? We get it at
369.141 or 370.312 cents, again always within a cent of just.

There is a humorous touch here, as I realized: in a certain
Pickwickian way, O3 might be said to observe the 2080/2079
distinguishing 99/80 or 9/8 plus 11/10 (368.914 cents), an
interval occurring in al-Farabi's 9:8-11:10-320:297, from 26/21 in
a permutation of Ibn Sina's 9:8-14:13-208:189, for example, as
well as his exquisite 8:7-13:12-14:13.

It is possible to view the smaller tempering of the submajor or
large neutral second at 369.141 cents as representing 99/80
(0.226 cents wide), and the larger at 370.312 cents as
representing 26/21. This kind of thing is a big part of my
culture of optimization, which should be fun!

The 14/11 major third is at 414.844 or 416.016 cents, the first
value actually leaning a bit toward 33/26 (412.745 cents), and
the second more strongly toward 14/11 (417.508 cents). These
results are fine, and subtly distinct from those of Peppermint
based on Keenan Pepper's Noble Fifth tuning (2/1, 704.096), where
in 1024-EDO, 14/11 is at 416.016 cents (as sometimes here) or the
virtually just 417.187 cents.

---------------------------------------------------------
2. Optimizing O3 in 1024-EDO: Setting the spacing and ZEO
---------------------------------------------------------

In the process of successive or layered optimization, we proceed
from the now-defined 12-note chain to the final parameter
defining O3 as a rank-3 tuning: the size of the spacing generator
between our established chain and the duplicate we are about to
add. In other words, what distance shall we place between the
chains.

Here two approaches happily coincide: eigenmonzos or ZEO
(Zalzalian Epimore Optimization). Note that 2010 was not yet
familiar with the meaning of the term eigenmonzo, although I seem
to recall hearing it various times on the tuning lists. However,
since "going for a just interval" is pretty much synonymous, I'll
use the RMP term, which I find very comfortable.

Apart from 22/21 and 26/21 -- and thus 13/11 -- my intended
eigenmonzos were 7/4, and also 11/6 (7/4 plus 22/21). Here
1024-EDO introduces a charming ambiguity and leeway: the "within
a cent or tuning unit" test for "virtual justness."

One form of virtual justness we have seen within a single chain,
specifically with 22/21, is always using the nearest
approximation (here 80.859 cents). A different form, which we
have seen with 13/11 and 26/21, where there are two tempered
sizes because of the inevitably irregular chain of fifths in a
1024-EDO "bitmap" or "halftoning pattern" to get the desired
shading of temperament, is having each of these sizes no further
than a 1024-EDO tuning unit (1.171875 cents) from just.

In other words, where there are two sizes, they should be the two
sizes with the just value in the middle: the two best 1024-EDO
approximations.

Accordingly, I optimized 7/4 knowing that the two best 1024-EDO
temperaments are 826 units at 967.969 cents (0.857 cents narrow),
and 827 units at 969.141 cents (0.315 cents wide).

Now in the 12-note O3 chain already defined, we have a major
sixth always within a cent of just of 22/13, at 777 units
(910.547 cents) or 778 units (911.719 cents). So a spacing of 49
units will make our 7/4 always 826 or 827 units, the two sizes
that bracket the just value of 968.826 cents.

How does our other eigenmonzo, 11/6, fare under this arrangement?
It's just value is 1049.363 cents, with the nearest 1024-EDO
values at either 895 units (1048.828 cents), 0.535 cents narrow;
or 896 units (1050.000 cents), 0.637 cents wide.

While we could calculate the spacing in terms of the regular
minor seventh at 846 or 847 units (991.406 or 992.578 cents,
knowing that the 22/21 limma or diatonic semitone is always at
its best approximation of 69 steps gives a shortcut: adding this
size of 69 steps to our 7/4 at 826 or 827 steps gives us our
desired 11/6 at 895 or 896 cents!

Our virtual eigenmonzos are thus in place. Now we come to a step
which has really already been resolved: ZEO, or checking the
accuracy of our four Zalzalian epimore steps, "Zalzalian" meaning
neutral steps or intervals, and referring to Mansur Zalzal, a
player of the `oud or lute in 8th-century Baghdad who is credited
with introducing the neutral third fret on this instrument.

Our 12-note chain has already determined the values for 14/13
(just size 128.298 cents) at 126.563 or 127.734 cents, always
within 1.736 cents or just; and 11/10, at a less ideal but
reasonably close representation of 161.719 cents or 3.285 cents
narrow. If both 11/10 and 14/13 were just, we would have a minor
third at 77/65 (293.302 cents), narrow of 32/27 by 2080/2079 or
0.833 cents. Each is a bit narrow, however, with the actual third
a near-just 13/11, or about a 352/351 (4.925 cents) smaller than
32/27 -- thus tempering out the difference between 352/351 or
2080/2079, or 847/845 (4.093 cents).

Having accounted for 14/13 and 11/10, the small and large neutral
steps, we have remaining the smaller and larger central steps at
13/12 and 12/11. The latter is always accounted for as the octave
inversion of our 11/6 eigenmonzo. Since 13/11 is also a "1024-EDO
eigenmonzo" always within a cent of just, it follows that 13/12
is likely near-just also. And so it is.

We know that a limma is always 69 units or 80.859 cents, and that
our optimal spacing for our other eigenmonzos such as 7/4 is
evidently 49 units or 57.422 cents. Adding these two intervals,
we find that a limma plus spacing will always be equal to 118
units or 138.281 cents -- a virtually just 13/12 at 138.573
cents!

So we have our temperament!

Here's a piece in it:

<http://www.bestII.com/~mschulter/Prelude_in_Shur_for_Erv_Wilson.mp3>

-----------------------------------------------
3. Jacques Dudon's influence: From O3 to MET-24
-----------------------------------------------

In the summer of 2011, Jacques Dudon and I had some discussions
in this group and elsewhere on his Tsaharuk system, in which he
stressed the importance of pure fifths and fourths as an ideal in
maqam. This led to a question: could I perhaps keep the
attractive features of O3 while reducing the temperament of the
fifths a bit? The just qanun tunings of Julien Jalaleddine Weiss
also served as an ideal which I might strive to approach a bit
more closely.

A related criterion was the wisdom of George Secor -- or my
sometimes curious version of it -- that a truly "near-just"
temperament ought to do significantly better with 3/2 and 4/3
than 12n-EDO. Peppermint, while a wonderful system, clearly
tempered the fifths and fourths at 2.141 cents, a bit _more_ than
12n-EDO, while O3 was in theory just about on par with 12n-EDO.

Of course, 29-HTT was my perennial inspiration, if "perennial"
means "since I learned about it from him in 2001." The thing was
that I wanted 14/13 and 14/11 just a bit closer to just than in
that classic system, but while still keeping some of the
"near-just" quality. Whatever I did, I would be standing on the
shoulders of a giant; but maybe I could add a small touch to make
the world of tunings yet more diverse.

Once I focused on the problem, 1024-EDO itself had an obvious
solution. As I've mentioned, there are two sizes of fifths
relevant for these temperaments of a kind we now call Parapyth:
a smaller fifth at 600 units or 703.125 cents, and a larger one
at 704.297 cents. We use a "bitmap" or "halftoning pattern" of
these two fifths to get a "shade of gray" somewhere in between.

The simplest such pattern would simply alternating a smaller
fifth with a larger one, and so filling out each 11-fifth chain!
The theoretical generator would thus be the average of the two
sizes, 703.711 cents, with maximal evenness: the whole-tone at
207.422 cents, and all intervals from even numbers of generators,
would have a single size, and likewise all intervals derived from
these plus or minus the spacing.

A simple and delightful bearing plan indeed:

703.1 704.3 703.1 704.3 703.1 704.3 703.1 704.3 703,1 704.3 703.1
Eb Bb F C G D A E B F# C# G#
600 601 600 601 600 601 600 601 600 601 600
+1 +2 +1 +2 +1 +2 +1 +2 +1 +2 +1

In some ways it brought to mind certain unequal temperaments of
Neidhardt in the 18th century alternating fifths tuned pure or
1/6-Pythagorean comma narrow to emulate a 1/12-Pythagorean comma
temperament, as in 12-EDO.

A big advantage was that a majority of fifths -- six out of 11,
are at 703.125 cents (1.170 cents wide), and thus substantially
closer to pure than 12n-EDO; while the others are not too much
more impure at 704.297 cents or 2.342 cents, by comparison with
1.955 cents. So I could call this "really near-just" in at least
a quasi-Secorian sense -- not necessarily to speak for George,
and while noting that it remains less "near-just" than 29-HTT at
703.579 cents!

The name I chose for the new tuning was Milder Extended
Temperament, or MET-24 -- milder, that is, than Peppermint or
even O3, with the fifths tempered in the wide or "extended"
direction (an idiom I learned from Jacques Dudon).

Since this is a rather small tweak of O3, lots of the features
remain the same. For example, 13/11 has the same sizes of around
288.3 or 289.5 cents, both within a cent of just. The spacing is
the same, 49 units or 57.422 cents. Let's consider a few subtle
changes.

First, from a ZEO perspective, this is the one 1024-EDO
Parapyth temperament of which I am aware (to use our new term)
where 14/13, 13/12, 12/11, and 11/10 are all consistently within
three cents of just.

This involves a compromise in which 11/10 is always formed from a
limma of 80.859 cents (the O3 value) or 82.031 cents, resulting
in a size of 162.891 cents, or 2.114 cents narrow -- well within
that HTT standard of 3.247 cents!

The real compromise, although not too severe is with 14/13, now a
bit smaller at 125.391 cents (2.908 cents narrow) or the size of
126.563 cents also found in O3 (1.736 cents narrow). So, on the
average, 14/13 is roughly as far from just as 11/10, a judicious
balance.

With 13/12 and 12/11, the changes from O3 are very subtle. While
13/12 was in O3 a virtual eigenmonzo with the single tempered size
closest to just (138.281 cents), here it fluctuates between this
size of 118 steps and the next larger at 119 steps of 139.453
cents -- 0.880 cents wide.

Likewise, 12/11 is very slightly less optimal, having a single
size of 150.000 cents, or 0.637 cents narrow -- rather than
varying between this size and the slightly more accurate value of
151.172 cents (0.535 cents wide). Since it is still always within
a tuning unit of just, it is still deemed a virtual eigenmonzo.

As in O3, 7/4 is always within a cent of just. The main and very
gentle "downside" is that 7/6 and 13/8 are consistently just over
2 cents from just, at 264.844 cents (2.027 cents narrow) and
842.578 cents (2.050 cents wide); whereas in O3, they have these
sizes, plus others closer to just at 266.016 cents (0.855 cents
narrow) and 841.406 cents (0.879 cents wide).

Thus MET-24 can be seen as a system willing to make small
compromises with other intervals in order to favor 3/2 and 4/3.
This is much the same kind of question as occurs in meantone,
with the philosophy of MET-24 about like this, "That temperament
which tempers slightly less may be tempering slightly better."

------------------------------------------------------------
4. Tuning culture and rank-3 spacing: Comparing ZEO and POTE
------------------------------------------------------------

A possible distinction between ZEO and allied techniques used in
the design of O3 and MET-24, and the RMP model with its POTE
optimization, is the influence of an epimore-oriented technique
on rank-3 spacing: the distance between the two chains of
fifths.

With ZEO, the ratios 12/11 and 13/12 have great weight; while
14/13 and -- in systems below 704 cents -- also 11/10 are of
interest, these arise from a single chain of fifths, rather than
from the third or spacing generator.

With POTE, if I understand it correctly, 11/8 and 13/8 would be
the primary goals, rather than 12/11 and 13/12 at respectively a
step lower on a chain of fifths all tempered in the wide
direction.

It is significant that in both O3 and in MET-24, 12/11 and 13/12
are always within a cent of just, while 11/8 and 13/8 have an
impurity typically of around 2-3 cents, with a greater weight
placed on 13/8, since it is more likely to arise above a drone in
a Near Eastern context than 11/8 for example. In both tunings,
13/8 is thus usually or always 2.050 cents wide; and 11/8 either
1.807 or 2.979 cents wide.

All these values are within three cents of just, or the HTT
tolerance of 3.247 cents. Yet epimores rather than primes are
clearly favored. Also, ratios of 7 are somewhat compromised in
favor of ratios of 11 and especially 13, with the about equal
impurity of 7/6 and 13/8 being a characteristic feature of these
tunings. This does not, however, favor 9/7, which is realized at
438.281 or 439.453 cents, respectively 3.197 or 4.369 cents wide
of pure (435.084 cents). The first is comparable to HTT-29
(438.332 cents, at the tolerance of 3.247 cents wide), but the
second and larger size more of a near-just 352/273 (440.009
cents) at a 352:351 wider than 9/7.

The overall effect of ZEO, and also the general guideline that
below 704 cents or so one tends to seek an eigenmonzo of 7/4
rather than 7/6 (a contrast in strategies exemplified by 29-HTT
and Peppermint), is to favor less spacing that one would find in
POTE Parapyth, with a difference on the order of 1-2 cents.

------------------------------------------------------------
5. Unintended consequences: approximations of 5-limit thirds
------------------------------------------------------------

One feature of the above optimization philosophy and process for
O3 and MET-24 would normally go without saying, but may bear
mention here: while the 11/10 large neutral second does play an
important rule in this optimization of a single 12-note chain,
and gives rise to some fascinating commas (either tempered out or
sometimes possibly "observed," as with the two values of 26/21 in
O3, both within a cent but the smaller yet better representing
99/80 at a 2080:2079 smaller), simple ratios of 5 are simply not
a consideration in the process.

Rather, a few small major and large minor thirds from the
augmented second (9 fifths up) plus spacing, or diminished fourth
(8 fourths up) less spacing, "go with the territory," much like
the diminished fourth or augmented second in 16th-century
meantone. Just as these meantone intervals were used for some
very striking special effects, but likely not seen as part of the
basic optimization process, so the near-5 thirds of O3 or MET-24
are seen as an incidental but enriching and diversifying aspect
of a mainly 2.3.7.11.13 system.

It is rather like setting the other parameters, many of them
described above, and then, as a sort of bonus, finding out which
shade of meantone-quality thirds one has picked out of the hat,
comparable to 1/5-comma or 1/6-comma in O3 and MET-24, and more
to 1/7-comma in Peppermint.

One point is that these approximate ratios of 5 -- for example
5/4 at 391.406 cents or 392.578 cents (5.093 or 6.264 cents wide)
in O3, the former size also appearing in MET-24 along with a
smaller one at 390.234 cents (3.921 cents wide) -- are not
related, at least in any simple and direct way, to the
optimization of the more complex ratio 11/10, also involving
prime 5. More indirectly, however, there is a certain connection.

When I say "at least in any direct or simple way," I mean that
the optimization for 11/10 involves a single 12-note chain of
fifths, while the incidental but predictable 5-limit or
meantone-quality thirds result from a more complicated
interaction of the linear generator (fifth or fourth) and the
spacing between chains.

Where the quest for 11/10 does play a role seems to be function
more generally of the quest for a large neutral second somewhat
larger than 160 cents (the value at an even 704 cents). Rather
than 11/10, for example, we might optimize for 208/189 at 165.837
cents, a ratio in Ibn Sina's tetrachord 9:8-14:13-208:189, with
identical results. This 13-limit ratio is actually larger than
11/10 by the small and friendly comma of 2080:2079 (0.833 cents),
but would still be within 3 cents of just in MET-24 at the value
used for 11/10, 162.891 cents (2.946 cents narrow of 208/189).
Thus optimizing 14/13, 13/12, 12/11, and 208/189 with all
consistently within 3 cents of just would define a 1024-EDO
tuning identical to that based on the kindred epimore 11/10.

The effect of this quest, be it for al-Farabi's 11/10 or Ibn
Sina's 208/189, is to favor a smaller linear generator, or more
precisely in 1024-EDO a bitmap or halftoning pattern with a smaller
average generator of 703.711 cents for O3.

This effect tends to favor somewhat more accurate 5-limit or
meantone-quality thirds, assuming a spacing for a pure 7/4,
simply because the size of the 63/52 small neutral third from
nine generators up grows or shrinks at rate nine times that of
the fifth, while that of the 22/13 major sixth changes at only
three times that of the fifth.

At 702.915 cents, a point well below 29-EDO (703.447 cents) and
the slightly higher range of O3 and MET-24, the diminished fifth
is a just 7/5 (582.512 cents), and this eigenmonzo makes it
possible for the same spacing to produce a just 5/4 and 7/4.
Taking the difference between our actual fifth and this size, and
multiplying the difference by six, will yield the impurity of 5/4
in the wide direction for a spacing at which 7/4 is pure.

For simplicity, let us calculate based on the average of our two
sizes of fifths in MET-24, 703.711 cents or 1201/2048 octave.
The difference from our 7/5 eigenmonzo fifth at 702.915 cents is
about 0.796 cents, with an impurity for 5/4 of 4.778 cents. In
practice, it is either 3.921 cents or 5.093 cents.

More specifically, a 63/52 augmented second tempered at 332.812
cents or 333.984 cents (just size 332.208 cents) plus the spacing
of 57.422 cents yields thirds of 390.234 cents or 391.406 cents.

While these are certainly pleasant meantone-quality shadings
interestingly filling a role analogous to the exotic remote
intervals of meantone, which might be used sparingly or
adventurously as an additional resource, another aspect of the
5-limit situation reveals a situation which, although a
consequence rather than a deliberate calculation of the
optimization process, seems felicitously to fit the ZEO ideal.

If we look at the basic 5-prime limit intervals of O3 or MET-24,
we find that the best is that of the epimore 10/9, used as a
melodic step in Ptolemy's Equable Diatonic 12:11:10:9 along with
the 12/11 and 11/10 steps included in the ZEO process. The 6/5
minor third is a bit less accurate, and 5/4 a bit yet less so --
a logical situation in a system where epimore steps are especially
favored, but not so much, I would guess, in a POTE optimization.

Looking at the chain of fifths for these 5-limit intervals in O3
and MET-24, with 27/20 also very accurate, may illustrate these
points. Here an asterisk (*) shows a note on the upper chain of
fifths raised by the rank-3 spacing generator.

O3 tuning system

680.449 182.404 884.359 386.314 1088.269
40/27 10/9 5/3 5/4 15/8
E* B* F#* C#* G#*
679.688 183.904 887.109 391.406 1095.703
-0.761 +1.581 +2.751 +5.093 -7.434

Bb
1/1
0

MET-24 tuning system

680.449 182.404 884.359 386.314 1088.269
40/27 10/9 5/3 5/4 15/8
E* B* F#* C#* G#*
679.688 183.904 887.109 391.406 1094.531
-0.761 +1.581 +2.751 +5.093 -6.263

Bb
1/1
0

All these intervals are of meantone quality in either tuning, not
as a feature of the design but as a natural consequence of that
design, with the near-just 10/9 step as a wonderful gift for
various ancient Greek and medieval Near Eastern tetrachords.
Another curious effect is that by the point where we reach 15/8,
the wide fifths have tempered this interval to the point where it
is a near-just 32/17 (just size 1095.445 cents). To a list of
commas tempered out, this adds 256/255 (6.776 cents), the
septendecimal kleisma or difference between 16/15 and 17/16.

In their role as rare and valued supplementary intervals, the 5/4
and 6/5 thirds would be fine in any shading from just to 12-EDO;
but, as it happens, the ZEO principle as applied to neutral
epimore steps, specifically 13/12 and 12/11, tends to keep these
5-limit intervals a bit closer to just, although I am only now
considering this relationship after over a year with MET-24!

One constraint on spacing is the precept: "Cherish and nurture
the 144/143," that is, the comma distinguishing a smaller central
neutral second at 13/12 from a larger one at 12/11. These steps
have just values of 138.573 and 150.637 cents, with the comma
thus at 12.064 cents. "Nurturing the 144/143" means trying to
keep it around this just size.

In 03, where 13/12 is always at its smaller 1024-EDO
approximation of 138.281 cents (also the more accurate one), this
precept is realized in almost ideal fashion: 12/11 is at 150.000
or 151.172 cents, and the comma thus at 10 or 11 tuning steps:
either 11.719 cents or 12.891 cents. Thus the 144/143 itself is,
so to speak, "virtually just."

In MET-24, there is a slight compromise: with 13/12 at either
138.281 or 139.453 cents, and 12/11 always at 150.000 cents, the
144/143 is tempered a bit on the narrow side at 10.547 or 11.719
cents. Here the interest is not only in keeping 144/143 as close
to just as possible, but in maintaining a certain degree of
subtle contrast between the smaller 13/12 and larger 12/11.

While the MET-24 compromise is quite acceptable one, enlarging
the spacing in this region (703.7-703.9 cents, say) to seek a
just 7/6 rather than a just 7/4, for example, would further
temper the 144/143 in the narrow direction by simultaneously
enlarging the 13/12 (limma plus spacing) and compressing the
12/11 (9/8 less spacing). The melodic imperative of ZEO, which
embraces not only epimore steps but commas, thus favors a
144/143-friendly spacing, with various ramifications either
calculated or simply accepted.

One of those ramifications which only this dialogue has called to
my attention is that the precepts of ZEO may actually tend to
improve 5-limit thirds, although this was not part of the
original calculation!

In going from Peppermint based on Keenan Pepper's Noble Fifth
tuning (2/1, 704.096, 58.680) to O3 and then MET-24, I noticed
that the 5-limit approximations seemed to be getting closer to
just, but did not look into the details.

However, as is now clear, both the choice of a smaller generator
(or average generator, in 1024-ED0) and ZEO spacing preferences
tend to improve these 5-limit thirds.

A possible further ramification might be that people who do not
share a musical outlook where the ZEO ethos is important, but who
do deliberately seek 5-limit thirds in Parapyth rank-3 systems of
this kind, might emulate a ZEO style of spacing (e.g. leaning
toward an eigenmonzo of 7/4 rather than 7/6 in the general range
of 703.6-703.9 cents) for the purpose of improving these thirds.

For someone coming from a ZEO ethos, the epimoric neutral steps
are the main point, with the more accurate 5-limit approximations
as an interesting ramification. For someone seeking a deliberate
5-limit optimization (possibly in a larger tuning size than 24),
the more accurate structure of superparticular or epimoric
neutral steps would likewise be an unintended although hopefully
not unpleasant consequence.

Most appreciatively,

Margo Schulter
October 31, 2012

11 in each chain, have three and only three JI sizes: 3/2, 273/242, or
44/39.

Also, as I'll discuss in another post, defining the large neutral step
at 162.891 cents as a tempering of Ibn Sina's 208/189 (the 32/27
complement of 14/13) rather than 11/10 might avoid a lot of
complications! In my tuning, 208/189 is still within 3 cents of just,
and given the tempering out of 352/351, my tempering could also
represent 169/154, for example (the difference of 13/11 and 14/13).

> I'm afraid I don't know what O3 is.

It's a temperament with a linear generator very close to the POTE, but
a bit less spacing: (2/1, 703.893, 57.148) in its theoretical form
with 21/11, 7/4, and 11/6 just. The 1024-EDO version has the 22 usual
fifths average out at 703.871 cents, again very close to the POTE, and
again with a bit narrower spacing (57.422 cents).

</tuning/topicId_91499.html#91499>
</tuning/topicId_105023.html#105224>

In fact, in my old-fashioned sense as well as the RMP sense of
Parapyth, O3 and the later MET-24 are simply two shadings of the same
basic temperament, with the latter seeking to go a bit easier on the
fifths and get a bit closer to the 165-cent region of large neutral
seconds (162.9 rather than 161.7 cents).

Comparing O3 and the POTE may be especially instructive because the
linear generators are almost identical, which lets us see what Ivor
Darreg might have called the advantages and disadvantages of different
nuances of spacing. What immediately appears is that the POTE is much
kinder to 9/7, and 2-3-7-9 intervals generally. A pure 7/6 would be
the minimax solution for these intervals, and the POTE gets closer
than O3, which is giving more weight to 13/8 and 11:12:13.

It's like a range of tastes in shades of meantone, but "with two
points in that space of tunings" -- linear generator and spacing,
assuming the octave is fixed at either 2/1 or TOP or whatever.

By the way, with your Cantonpenta, I noticed you chose 271-EDO, which
has an outstanding fit, but curiously with a narrowish spacing at
57.565 cents -- which this EDO pretty much selects for us. Humorously,
I wondered if this could almost be an example my style of spacing
maybe carried a bit further: it does wonders for 11/8, 13/8, and 11/6,
and actually in this range right around a just 14/13 is more sparing
of 9/7 than around MET-24 (703.711 cents) or even O3 (703.893 cents).

What I did to get a possible 34-note parapyth superset of Cantonpenta
in 271-EDO was to recognize your scale as a subset of a 17-MOS,
generate the 17-MOS, and then set a spacing of 13 steps of 271-EDO for
a second chain.

<http://www.bestII.com/~mschulter/cantonpentalike34.scl>

Did I get this right? If so, you're welcome to adopt it as a
Cantonpenta variation.

Best,

Margo

Ah. In my vocabulary, that makes it a tuning of parapyth temperament, specifically the one with 21/11, 7/4 and 11/6 as eigenmonzos, or equivalently you can just say 2, 7 and 11/3. One nice thing about transversals is you can take the transversal and put into POTE, O3 or any other parapyth tuning which strikes your fancy.

I'm not sure what you mean by "right"; it's certainly a reasonable thing to do, and 271et is clearly a possible system to use for parapyth and related temperaments. Whether the result is a Fokker block or not I'd need to analyze to tell, but either way it makes sense.
